The alliance between the Western Allies and the Soviet Union had begun to deteriorate even before the war was over.[\[343\]](#cite_note-Kantowicz_2000_6-346)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/EasternBloc_BorderChange38-48.svg/250px-EasternBloc_BorderChange38-48.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:EasternBloc_BorderChange38-48.svg)

Post-war border changes in [Central Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Europe "Central Europe") and creation of the [Communist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist "Communist") [Eastern Bloc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Bloc "Eastern Bloc")

Besides Germany, the rest of Europe was also divided into Western and Soviet [spheres of influence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spheres_of_influence "Spheres of influence").[\[344\]](#cite_note-Trachtenberg_1999_33-347) Most eastern and central European countries fell into the [Soviet sphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Bloc "Eastern Bloc"), which led to the establishment of Communist-led regimes, with full or partial support of the Soviet occupation authorities. As a result, [East Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Germany "East Germany"),[\[345\]](#cite_note-Applebaum_2012-348) [Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_People%27s_Republic "Polish People's Republic"), [Hungary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungarian_People%27s_Republic "Hungarian People's Republic"), [Romania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Romania "Socialist Republic of Romania"), [Bulgaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Bulgaria "People's Republic of Bulgaria"), [Czechoslovakia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czechoslovak_Socialist_Republic "Czechoslovak Socialist Republic"), and [Albania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Socialist_Republic_of_Albania "People's Socialist Republic of Albania")[\[346\]](#cite_note-Naimark_2010-349) became Soviet [satellite states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satellite_state#Soviet_satellite_states "Satellite state"). Communist [Yugoslavia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia "Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia") conducted a fully [independent policy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement "Non-Aligned Movement"), causing [tension with the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tito%E2%80%93Stalin_split "Tito–Stalin split").[\[347\]](#cite_note-Swain_1992-350) A [communist uprising in Greece](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_Civil_War "Greek Civil War") was put down with Anglo-American support and the country remained aligned with the West.[\[348\]](#cite_note-351)

Post-war division of the world was formalised by two international military alliances, the United States-led [NATO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO "NATO") and the Soviet-led [Warsaw Pact](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw_Pact "Warsaw Pact").[\[349\]](#cite_note-Borstelmann_2005_318-352) The long period of political tensions and military competition between them—the [Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War")—would be accompanied by an unprecedented [arms race](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arms_race "Arms race") and a number of [proxy wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proxy_war "Proxy war") throughout the world.[\[350\]](#cite_note-353)

In Asia, the United States led the [occupation of Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occupation_of_Japan "Occupation of Japan") and [administered Japan's former islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trust_Territory_of_the_Pacific_Islands "Trust Territory of the Pacific Islands") in the Western Pacific, while the Soviets annexed [South Sakhalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Sakhalin "South Sakhalin") and the [Kuril Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuril_Islands "Kuril Islands").[\[351\]](#cite_note-Weinberg_2005_911-354) [Korea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Korea "Korea"), formerly [under Japanese colonial rule](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Korea_under_Japanese_rule "Korea under Japanese rule"), was [divided and occupied](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Division_of_Korea "Division of Korea") by the Soviet Union in the [North](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Korea "North Korea") and the United States in the [South](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Korea "South Korea") between 1945 and 1948. Separate republics emerged on both sides of the 38th parallel in 1948, each claiming to be the legitimate government for all of Korea, which led ultimately to the [Korean War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Korean_War "Korean War").[\[352\]](#cite_note-355)

In China, nationalist and communist forces resumed [the civil war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War "Chinese Civil War") in June 1946. Communist forces prevailed and established the People's Republic of China on the mainland, while nationalist forces retreated to [Taiwan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwan "Taiwan") in 1949.[\[353\]](#cite_note-Lynch_2010_12_13-356) In the Middle East, the Arab rejection of the [United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine "United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine") and the [creation of Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Creation_of_Israel "Creation of Israel") marked the escalation of the [Arab–Israeli conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict "Arab–Israeli conflict"). While European powers attempted to retain some or all of their [colonial empires](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonial_empire "Colonial empire"), their losses of prestige and resources during the war rendered this unsuccessful, leading to [decolonisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decolonisation "Decolonisation").[\[354\]](#cite_note-JMRoberts_1996_589-357)[\[355\]](#cite_note-358)

The global economy suffered heavily from the war, although participating nations were affected differently. The United States emerged much richer than any other nation, leading to a [baby boom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mid-20th_century_baby_boom "Mid-20th century baby boom"), and by 1950 its [gross domestic product](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gross_domestic_product "Gross domestic product") per person was much greater than that of any of the other powers, and it dominated the world economy.[\[356\]](#cite_note-359) The Allied occupational authorities pursued a policy of [industrial disarmament in Western Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allied_plans_for_German_industry_after_World_War_II "Allied plans for German industry after World War II") from 1945 to 1948.[\[357\]](#cite_note-Balabkins_1964_207-360) Due to international trade interdependencies, this policy led to an economic stagnation in Europe and delayed European recovery from the war for several years.[\[358\]](#cite_note-361)[\[359\]](#cite_note-Balabkins_1964_208,209-362)

At the [Bretton Woods Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bretton_Woods_Conference "Bretton Woods Conference") in July 1944, the Allied nations drew up an economic framework for the post-war world. The agreement created the [International Monetary Fund](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund "International Monetary Fund") (IMF) and the [International Bank for Reconstruction and Development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development "International Bank for Reconstruction and Development") (IBRD), which later became part of the [World Bank Group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Bank_Group "World Bank Group"). The [Bretton Woods system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bretton_Woods_system "Bretton Woods system") lasted until 1973.[\[360\]](#cite_note-363) Recovery began with the mid-1948 [currency reform in West Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deutsche_Mark "Deutsche Mark"), and was sped up by the liberalisation of European economic policy that the US [Marshall Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marshall_Plan "Marshall Plan") economic aid (1948–1951) both directly and indirectly caused.[\[361\]](#cite_note-364)[\[362\]](#cite_note-Balabkins_1964_212-365) The post-1948 West German recovery has been called the [German economic miracle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wirtschaftswunder#West_Germany "Wirtschaftswunder").[\[363\]](#cite_note-366) Italy also experienced an [economic boom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_economic_miracle "Italian economic miracle")[\[364\]](#cite_note-367) and the [French economy rebounded](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trente_Glorieuses "Trente Glorieuses").[\[365\]](#cite_note-368) By contrast, the United Kingdom was in a state of economic ruin,[\[366\]](#cite_note-369) and although receiving a quarter of the total Marshall Plan assistance, more than any other European country,[\[367\]](#cite_note-370) it continued in relative economic decline for decades.[\[368\]](#cite_note-371) The Soviet Union, despite enormous human and material losses, also experienced rapid increases in production in the immediate post-war era,[\[369\]](#cite_note-Smith_1993_32-372) having seized and transferred most of Germany's industrial plants and exacted [war reparations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II_reparations "World War II reparations") from its satellite states.[\[d\]](#cite_note-373)[\[370\]](#cite_note-374) Japan recovered much later.[\[371\]](#cite_note-375) China returned to its pre-war industrial production by 1952.[\[372\]](#cite_note-376)

## Impact

### Casualties

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Nanking_bodies_1937.jpg/250px-Nanking_bodies_1937.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Nanking_bodies_1937.jpg)

Bodies of Chinese civilians killed by the [Imperial Japanese Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Army "Imperial Japanese Army") during the [Nanjing Massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nanjing_Massacre "Nanjing Massacre") in December 1937

An estimated 60 million to more than 75 million people died in the war including at least 20 million who died from deprivation, famine and disease.[\[373\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor20121-377)[\[374\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHastings2011669–670-378)[\[375\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAubinBernardGuillerat2019147-379)[\[376\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanson2017470-380) Civilian deaths have been estimated to comprise 67%[\[377\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClodfelter2017528-381) to 80%[\[378\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanson201738-382) of all direct and indirect deaths from the war. The Soviet Union had the highest overall death toll (estimated at 20 million to 28 million),[\[379\]](#cite_note-383) followed by China (at least 15 million),[\[374\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHastings2011669–670-378)[\[380\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanson2017487-384)[\[381\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAubinBernardGuillerat2019146-385) Germany (6 million to 8.7 million)[\[382\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanson2017488-386)[\[381\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAubinBernardGuillerat2019146-385) and Poland (5 million to 6.5 million).[\[374\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHastings2011669–670-378)[\[381\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAubinBernardGuillerat2019146-385)

The countries which sustained the most military deaths were the Soviet Union (about 8.7 million),[\[383\]](#cite_note-Ell&Mak_19942-387) Germany (around 5.3 million),[\[384\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAubinBernardGuillerat2019152-388) China (2 million to 3 million)[\[385\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMitter2013381-389)[\[386\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAubinBernardGuillerat2019148-390) and Japan (1.7 million to 2.5 million).[\[374\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHastings2011669–670-378)[\[386\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAubinBernardGuillerat2019148-390) Of the 20 million to 25 million military deaths in the war, the majority were of German and Soviet soldiers, including prisoners of war (POWs), on the Eastern Front.[\[387\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanson2017473-391)

The high civilian death toll relative to military deaths was unusual for major wars up to that time.[\[388\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanson2017469-392) Some 10 million to 15 million people died of starvation and disease in China and the Soviet Union, and 8 million to 10 million in India and under Japanese occupation elsewhere in Asia and the Pacific.[\[389\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanson2017472–473-393) Around 15 million civilians died in genocides and other deliberate killings, while millions in total died in concentration camps, aerial bombings and in combat zones.[\[390\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanson2017474–475,_481–485-394)

### Genocide, war crimes, and crimes against humanity

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Czeslawa_Kwoka_-_Brasse.jpg/250px-Czeslawa_Kwoka_-_Brasse.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Czeslawa_Kwoka_-_Brasse.jpg)

[Prisoner identity photograph of a Polish girl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czes%C5%82awa_Kwoka "Czesława Kwoka") taken by the German [SS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SS "SS") in [Auschwitz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auschwitz "Auschwitz").[\[391\]](#cite_note-395) Approximately 230,000 children were held prisoner and used in forced labour and [Nazi medical experiments](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_medical_experiments "Nazi medical experiments").

In [trials following the war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Axis_war_crime_trials "List of Axis war crime trials"), representatives of the Axis powers and their accomplices were convicted of numerous [war crimes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_crime "War crime"), [crimes against humanity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity "Crimes against humanity") and complicity in [genocides](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genocide "Genocide").[\[392\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2014-396) The Nazis killed about 6 million Jews in a racially motivated genocide known as the [Holocaust](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocaust "Holocaust"). They also killed millions of [Slavs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slavs "Slavs"), over 130 thousand [Romani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romani_people "Romani people"), and members of other groups that they considered racially inferior.[\[393\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanson2017474–477-397)[\[394\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200055–60-398) Almost 300,000 people with mental and physical disabilities were also [systematically killed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aktion_T4 "Aktion T4") in Germany and its occupied territories.[\[395\]](#cite_note-399)

The killing of civilians and POWs through massacres and deliberate starvation was especially common in the Eastern European and Asia-Pacific theatres. German forces on the Eastern Front destroyed or confiscated available food, massacred civilians in reprisals and routinely shot prisoners.[\[396\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanson2017471–472-400)[\[392\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2014-396) The Japanese killed millions of civilians in occupied areas through massacres and [scorched earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scorched_earth "Scorched earth") strategies; for example, in their "[kill all, burn all, loot all](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Three_Alls_policy "Three Alls policy")" policy in China.[\[397\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanson2017470–472-401)[\[398\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMitter2013289–290-402) In the [Nanking Massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nanking_Massacre "Nanking Massacre"), between 40,000 and 200,000 Chinese civilians and POWs were killed.[\[399\]](#cite_note-:04-403) Japan also [used biological weapons in China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unit_731 "Unit 731") and in [early conflicts against the Soviets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battles_of_Khalkhin_Gol "Battles of Khalkhin Gol").[\[400\]](#cite_note-:43-404)[\[401\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHastings2011428–429-405) The Soviet Union was responsible for imprisoning, deporting and often [executing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NKVD_prisoner_massacres "NKVD prisoner massacres") hundreds of thousands of civilians and POWs from occupied or annexed territories.**[\[402\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAkashiDaviesService2014-406)**[\[403\]](#cite_note-:47-407) This included the [Katyn massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katyn_massacre "Katyn massacre") of 22,000 Polish officers and intellectuals.[\[404\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDimbleby202281–82-408)

War crimes were also committed in civil wars and conflicts between resistance groups in occupied territories. In Yugoslavia, numerous war crimes, including the massacre of civilians and prisoners, were committed by Axis forces and the Axis-aligned Croatian [Ustaše](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Usta%C5%A1e "Ustaše"). The main resistance groups, the Serbian-Nationalist [Chetniks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chetniks "Chetniks") and the Communist-led [partisans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yugoslav_Partisans "Yugoslav Partisans"), also committed massacres and persecutions of their enemies.[\[392\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2014-396)[\[405\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2014-409) In Poland, about 100,000 Poles were killed by the [Ukrainian Insurgent Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_Insurgent_Army "Ukrainian Insurgent Army") in the [Volhynia massacres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volhynia_massacres "Volhynia massacres") between 1943 and 1945. About 10,000 Ukrainians were killed by Poles in reprisal attacks.[\[406\]](#cite_note-410) In Greece, Axis forces were mainly responsible for civilian deaths through deliberate starvation and reprisal massacres, although the major resistance forces, [ELAS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ELAS "ELAS") and [EDES](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/EDES "EDES"), also committed war crimes.[\[407\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClogg2014-411)[\[392\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2014-396)

The Soviet Union, Japan and Germany inflicted high death rates on POWs through executions, starvation, forced labour and other mistreatment. The Soviet Union and Japan had not ratified the [Geneva Convention on Prisoners of War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geneva_Convention_on_Prisoners_of_War "Geneva Convention on Prisoners of War"), and Germany regarded itself as exempt from the convention on the Eastern Front.[\[392\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2014-396) About a third of those taken prisoner by the Japanese died, as did almost 60 per cent of Soviet prisoners of the Germans. About a third of Germans taken prisoner by the Soviet Union died in captivity. The mortality rate of German and Japanese prisoners of the Western allies was 1 to 2 per cent.[\[408\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHanson2017482-412)[\[409\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDimbleby2022501-413)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/The_Liberation_of_Bergen-belsen_Concentration_Camp%2C_April_1945_BU4031.jpg/250px-The_Liberation_of_Bergen-belsen_Concentration_Camp%2C_April_1945_BU4031.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_Liberation_of_Bergen-belsen_Concentration_Camp,_April_1945_BU4031.jpg)

[Schutzstaffel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schutzstaffel "Schutzstaffel") (SS) women camp guards removing prisoners' bodies from lorries and carrying them to a mass grave, inside the German [Bergen-Belsen concentration camp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bergen-Belsen_concentration_camp "Bergen-Belsen concentration camp"), 1945

Germany, Japan and the Soviet Union made extensive use of forced labour of foreign civilians and POWs. In greater Germany, there were 7.6 million foreign workers (including POWs undertaking forced labour) and about 500,000 slave labourers in concentration camps by late 1944.[\[410\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerbert2014-414) Those civilians and POWs from Soviet-occupied territories who were deported to the Soviet Union were usually imprisoned in the Soviet forced labour camps, known as the [gulag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulag "Gulag")**.[\[402\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAkashiDaviesService2014-406)** Between 200,000 and one million Soviet POWs and civilians repatriated from German camps were also sent to the gulag as alleged Axis collaborators[\[411\]](#cite_note-:61-415)[\[392\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2014-396) where many died from malnutrition, the harsh climate and overwork.**[\[403\]](#cite_note-:47-407)[\[402\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAkashiDaviesService2014-406)** The Japanese conscripted millions of foreign civilians and POWs to undertake forced labour in Japan and its occupied territories where they suffered harsh treatment and high death rates.[\[412\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKratoska2015xv-416)[\[413\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJacob20185–7-417) Up to 200,000 Korean and Chinese women were forced into sex slavery.[\[414\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJacob20186-418)

While troops of all the major belligerents committed rapes, the rape of civilians was particularly widespread among the German, Japanese and Soviet military. The post-war international military tribunals found the evidence of rape by German forces "overwhelming". Twenty-nine Japanese defendants, mostly generals, were convicted of complicity in mass rape.[\[415\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeumann2013553–554-419) Soviet soldiers also committed mass rapes in occupied territories, especially Germany.[\[416\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTECherry2013556–557-420)[\[417\]](#cite_note-Bird-421)

War crimes were committed by the Western Allied powers, but not on the same scale as those of the Axis powers and the Soviet Union.[\[392\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2014-396) The Western Allies prosecuted a number of war crimes committed by their own forces, but Allied war crimes were not prosecuted by the post-war international military tribunals.[\[418\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHastings2011445–446,_671–672-422)[\[392\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2014-396) There has been continued debate over whether the [area bombing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Area_bombing "Area bombing") of cities in Germany and Japan, and the [atomic bombing of Hiroshima and Nagasaki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_bombing_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki "Atomic bombing of Hiroshima and Nagasaki"), were war crimes.[\[419\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrayling20141–2-423)[\[392\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2014-396)

### Occupation

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Palmiry_before_execution.jpg/250px-Palmiry_before_execution.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Palmiry_before_execution.jpg)

Polish civilians wearing blindfolds photographed just before being massacred by German soldiers in [Palmiry forest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palmiry_massacre "Palmiry massacre"), 1940

In Europe, occupation came under two forms. In Western, Northern, and Central Europe (France, Norway, Denmark, the Low Countries, and the [annexed portions of Czechoslovakia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protectorate_of_Bohemia_and_Moravia "Protectorate of Bohemia and Moravia")) Germany established economic policies through which it collected roughly 69.5 billion reichsmarks (27.8 billion US dollars) by the end of the war; this figure does not include the [plunder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_plunder "Nazi plunder") of industrial products, military equipment, raw materials and other goods.[\[420\]](#cite_note-424) Thus, the income from occupied nations was over 40 percent of the income Germany collected from taxation, a figure which increased to nearly 40 percent of total German income as the war went on.[\[421\]](#cite_note-Milward_1979_138-425)

In the East, the intended gains of _[Lebensraum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebensraum "Lebensraum")_ were never attained as fluctuating front-lines and Soviet [scorched earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scorched_earth "Scorched earth") policies denied resources to the German invaders.[\[422\]](#cite_note-Milward_1992_148-426) Unlike in the West, the [Nazi racial policy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_racial_policy "Nazi racial policy") encouraged extreme brutality against what it considered to be the "[inferior people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Untermensch "Untermensch")" of [Slavic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slavic_peoples "Slavic peoples") descent; most German advances were thus followed by [mass atrocities and war crimes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Generalplan_Ost "Generalplan Ost").[\[423\]](#cite_note-427) The Nazis [killed an estimated 2.8 million ethnic Poles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_crimes_against_the_Polish_nation "Nazi crimes against the Polish nation") in addition to Polish-Jewish [victims of the Holocaust](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Victims_of_the_Holocaust "Victims of the Holocaust").[\[424\]](#cite_note-428) Although by 1942 [resistance groups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resistance_during_World_War_II "Resistance during World War II") formed in most occupied territories,[\[425\]](#cite_note-429) the assessments of the effectiveness of [Soviet partisans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_partisans "Soviet partisans")[\[426\]](#cite_note-430) and [French Resistance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Resistance "French Resistance")[\[427\]](#cite_note-431) suggests that they did not significantly hamper German operations until late 1943.

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-031-2436-03A%2C_Russland%2C_Hinrichtung_von_Partisanen_retouched.jpg/250px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-031-2436-03A%2C_Russland%2C_Hinrichtung_von_Partisanen_retouched.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-031-2436-03A,_Russland,_Hinrichtung_von_Partisanen_retouched.jpg)

[Soviet partisans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_partisans "Soviet partisans") hanged by the German army. The [Russian Academy of Sciences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Academy_of_Sciences "Russian Academy of Sciences") reported in 1995 that [civilian victims in the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II_casualties_of_the_Soviet_Union "World War II casualties of the Soviet Union") at German hands totalled 13.7 million dead, twenty percent of the 68 million people in the occupied Soviet Union.

In Asia, Japan termed nations under its occupation as being part of the [Greater East Asia Co-Prosperity Sphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_East_Asia_Co-Prosperity_Sphere "Greater East Asia Co-Prosperity Sphere"), essentially a Japanese [hegemony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hegemony "Hegemony") which it claimed was for purposes of liberating colonised peoples.[\[428\]](#cite_note-432) Although Japanese forces were sometimes welcomed as liberators from European domination, [Japanese war crimes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_war_crimes "Japanese war crimes") frequently turned local public opinion against them.[\[429\]](#cite_note-GSWW6_266-433) During Japan's initial conquest, it captured 4,000,000 barrels (640,000 m3) of oil (~550,000 tonnes) left behind by retreating Allied forces; and by 1943, was able to get production in the Dutch East Indies up to 50 million barrels (7,900,000 m3) of oil (~6.8 million tonnes), 76 percent of its 1940 output rate.[\[429\]](#cite_note-GSWW6_266-433)

### Home fronts and production

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/World_War_II_Allies_to_Axis_GDP_Ratio.svg/500px-World_War_II_Allies_to_Axis_GDP_Ratio.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:World_War_II_Allies_to_Axis_GDP_Ratio.svg)

Allies to Axis GDP ratio throughout the war

In the 1930s, Britain and the United States together controlled almost 75% of world mineral output—essential for projecting military power.[\[430\]](#cite_note-434)

In Europe, before the outbreak of the war, the Allies had significant advantages in both population and economics. In 1938, the Western Allies (United Kingdom, France, Poland and the British Dominions) had a 30 percent larger population and a 30 percent higher gross domestic product than the European Axis powers (Germany and Italy); including colonies, the Allies had more than a 5:1 advantage in population and a nearly 2:1 advantage in GDP.[\[431\]](#cite_note-6Econ3-435) In Asia at the same time, China had roughly six times the population of Japan but only an 89 percent higher GDP; this reduces to three times the population and only a 38 percent higher GDP if Japanese colonies are included.[\[431\]](#cite_note-6Econ3-435)

The United States produced about two-thirds of all munitions used by the Allies in World War II, including warships, transports, warplanes, artillery, tanks, trucks, and ammunition.[\[432\]](#cite_note-436) Although the Allies' economic and population advantages were largely mitigated during the initial rapid blitzkrieg attacks of Germany and Japan, they became the decisive factor by 1942, after the United States and Soviet Union joined the Allies and the war evolved into one of [attrition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attrition_warfare "Attrition warfare").[\[433\]](#cite_note-6Econ2-437) While the Allies' ability to out-produce the Axis was partly due to more access to natural resources, other factors, such as Germany and Japan's reluctance to employ women in the [labour force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labour_force "Labour force"),[\[434\]](#cite_note-438) Allied [strategic bombing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strategic_bombing_during_World_War_II "Strategic bombing during World War II"),[\[435\]](#cite_note-439) and Germany's late shift to a [war economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_economy "War economy")[\[436\]](#cite_note-440) contributed significantly. Additionally, neither Germany nor Japan planned to fight a protracted war, and had not equipped themselves to do so.[\[437\]](#cite_note-441) Germany, Japan and the Soviet Union used millions of [slave labourers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slavery "Slavery") in war-related industries.[\[410\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerbert2014-414)[\[412\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKratoska2015xv-416)[\[392\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2014-396)

### Advances in technology and its application

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1978-Anh.026-01%2C_Peenem%C3%BCnde%2C_V2_beim_Start.jpg/250px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1978-Anh.026-01%2C_Peenem%C3%BCnde%2C_V2_beim_Start.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1978-Anh.026-01,_Peenem%C3%BCnde,_V2_beim_Start.jpg)

A [V-2 rocket](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/V-2_rocket "V-2 rocket") launched from a fixed site in [Peenemünde](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peenem%C3%BCnde "Peenemünde"), 21 June 1943

Aircraft were used for [reconnaissance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reconnaissance_aircraft "Reconnaissance aircraft"), as [fighters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fighter_aircraft "Fighter aircraft"), [bombers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bomber "Bomber"), and [ground-support](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Close_air_support "Close air support"), and each role developed considerably. Innovations included [airlift](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airlift "Airlift") (the capability to quickly move limited high-priority supplies, equipment, and personnel);[\[438\]](#cite_note-EncWWII_76-442) and [strategic bombing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strategic_bombing "Strategic bombing") (the bombing of enemy industrial and population centres to destroy the enemy's ability to wage war).[\[439\]](#cite_note-443) [Anti-aircraft weaponry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-aircraft_weaponry "Anti-aircraft weaponry") also advanced, including defences such as [radar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radar "Radar") and surface-to-air artillery, in particular the introduction of the [proximity fuze](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proximity_fuze "Proximity fuze"). The use of the [jet aircraft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jet_aircraft "Jet aircraft") was pioneered and led to jets becoming standard in air forces worldwide.[\[440\]](#cite_note-444)

Advances were made in nearly every aspect of [naval warfare](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naval_warfare "Naval warfare"), most notably with [aircraft carriers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aircraft_carrier "Aircraft carrier") and [submarines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Submarine "Submarine"). Although [aeronautical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aeronautical "Aeronautical") warfare had relatively little success at the start of the war, [actions at Taranto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Taranto "Battle of Taranto"), [Pearl Harbor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor "Attack on Pearl Harbor"), and the [Coral Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_the_Coral_Sea "Battle of the Coral Sea") established the carrier as the dominant capital ship (in place of the battleship).[\[441\]](#cite_note-EncWWII_163-445)[\[442\]](#cite_note-446)[\[443\]](#cite_note-447) In the Atlantic, [escort carriers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Escort_carrier "Escort carrier") became a vital part of Allied convoys, increasing the effective protection radius and helping to close the [Mid-Atlantic gap](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_gap "Mid-Atlantic gap").[\[444\]](#cite_note-448) Carriers were also more economical than [battleships](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battleship "Battleship") due to the relatively low cost of aircraft[\[445\]](#cite_note-449) and because they are not required to be as heavily armoured.[\[446\]](#cite_note-450) Submarines, which had proved to be an effective weapon during the [First World War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_World_War "First World War"),[\[447\]](#cite_note-Bur&Ryd_1995_15-451) were expected by all combatants to be important in the second. The British focused development on [anti-submarine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-submarine_warfare "Anti-submarine warfare") [weaponry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-submarine_weapon "Anti-submarine weapon") and tactics, such as [sonar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sonar "Sonar") and convoys, while Germany focused on improving its offensive capability, with designs such as the [Type VII submarine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Type_VII_submarine "Type VII submarine") and [wolfpack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wolfpack_\(naval_tactic\) "Wolfpack (naval tactic)") tactics.[\[448\]](#cite_note-Bur&Ryd_1995_16-452) Gradually, improving Allied technologies such as the [Leigh Light](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leigh_Light "Leigh Light"), [Hedgehog](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hedgehog_\(weapon\) "Hedgehog (weapon)"), [Squid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Squid_\(weapon\) "Squid (weapon)"), and [homing torpedoes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_24_mine "Mark 24 mine") proved effective against German submarines.[\[449\]](#cite_note-453)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Trinity_device_readied.jpg/250px-Trinity_device_readied.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Trinity_device_readied.jpg)

Nuclear _Gadget_ being raised to the top of the detonation "shot tower", at [Alamogordo Bombing Range](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alamogordo_Bombing_and_Gunnery_Range "Alamogordo Bombing and Gunnery Range"); [Trinity nuclear test](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trinity_nuclear_test "Trinity nuclear test"), [New Mexico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Mexico "New Mexico"), July 1945

[Land warfare](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_warfare "Land warfare") changed from the static frontlines of [trench warfare](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trench_warfare "Trench warfare") of World War I, which had relied on improved [artillery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artillery "Artillery") that outmatched the speed of both [infantry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infantry "Infantry") and [cavalry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cavalry "Cavalry"), to increased mobility and [combined arms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Combined_arms "Combined arms"). The [tank](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tank "Tank"), which had been used predominantly for infantry support in the First World War, had evolved into the primary weapon.[\[450\]](#cite_note-EncWWII_125-454) In the late 1930s, tank design was considerably more advanced than it had been during World War I,[\[451\]](#cite_note-455) and [advances continued throughout the war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tanks_in_World_War_II "Tanks in World War II") with increases in speed, armour and firepower.[\[452\]](#cite_note-456)[\[453\]](#cite_note-457) At the start of the war, most commanders thought enemy tanks should be met by tanks with superior specifications.[\[454\]](#cite_note-EncWWII_108-458) This idea was challenged by the poor performance of the relatively light early tank guns against armour, and German doctrine of avoiding tank-versus-tank combat. This, along with Germany's use of combined arms, were among the key elements of their highly successful blitzkrieg tactics across Poland and France.[\[450\]](#cite_note-EncWWII_125-454) Many means of [destroying tanks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-tank_warfare "Anti-tank warfare"), including [indirect artillery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indirect_fire "Indirect fire"), [anti-tank guns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-tank_gun "Anti-tank gun") (both towed and [self-propelled](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-propelled_artillery "Self-propelled artillery")), [mines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-tank_mine "Anti-tank mine"), short-ranged infantry antitank weapons, and other tanks were used.[\[454\]](#cite_note-EncWWII_108-458) Even with large-scale mechanisation, infantry remained the backbone of all forces,[\[455\]](#cite_note-EncWWII_734-459) and throughout the war, most infantry were equipped similarly to World War I.[\[456\]](#cite_note-Comp_221-460) The portable machine gun spread, a notable example being the German [MG 34](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MG_34 "MG 34"), and various [submachine guns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Submachine_gun "Submachine gun") which were suited to [close combat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Close_combat "Close combat") in urban and jungle settings.[\[456\]](#cite_note-Comp_221-460) The [assault rifle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assault_rifle "Assault rifle"), a late war development incorporating many features of the rifle and submachine gun, became the standard post-war infantry weapon for most armed forces.[\[457\]](#cite_note-461)

Most major belligerents attempted to solve the problems of complexity and security involved in using large [codebooks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Codebook "Codebook") for [cryptography](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptography "Cryptography") by designing [ciphering](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cipher "Cipher") machines, the most well-known being the German [Enigma machine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enigma_machine "Enigma machine").[\[458\]](#cite_note-462) Development of [SIGINT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SIGINT "SIGINT") (_sig_nals _int_elligence) and [cryptanalysis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptanalysis "Cryptanalysis") enabled the countering process of decryption. Notable examples were the Allied decryption of [Japanese naval codes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_naval_codes "Japanese naval codes")[\[459\]](#cite_note-Schoenherr-463) and British [Ultra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultra_\(cryptography\) "Ultra (cryptography)"), a [pioneering method](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bombe#The_British_Bombe "Bombe") for decoding Enigma that benefited from information given to the United Kingdom by the [Polish Cipher Bureau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cipher_Bureau_\(Poland\)#Gift_to_allies "Cipher Bureau (Poland)"), which had been decoding early versions of Enigma before the war.[\[460\]](#cite_note-464) Another component of [military intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_intelligence "Military intelligence") was [deception](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deception "Deception"), which the Allies used to great effect in operations such as [Mincemeat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Mincemeat "Operation Mincemeat") and [Bodyguard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Bodyguard "Operation Bodyguard").[\[459\]](#cite_note-Schoenherr-463)[\[461\]](#cite_note-465)

Other technological and engineering feats achieved during, or as a result of, the war include the world's first programmable computers ([Z3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Z3_\(computer\) "Z3 (computer)"), [Colossus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colossus_computer "Colossus computer"), and [ENIAC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ENIAC "ENIAC")), [guided missiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/V-1_flying_bomb "V-1 flying bomb") and [modern rockets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/V-2_rocket "V-2 rocket"), the [Manhattan Project](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manhattan_Project "Manhattan Project")'s development of [nuclear weapons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_weapon "Nuclear weapon"), [operations research](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operations_research "Operations research"), the development of [artificial harbours](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mulberry_harbour "Mulberry harbour"), and [oil pipelines under the English Channel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Pluto "Operation Pluto").[\[462\]](#cite_note-466)[\[463\]](#cite_note-467) Although [penicillin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Penicillin "Penicillin") was discovered before the war, the [development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_penicillin "History of penicillin") of industrial production technology as well as the mass production and use began during the war.[\[464\]](#cite_note-468)

## Notes

1.  **[^](#cite_ref-1)** While [various other dates](#Start_and_end_dates) have been proposed as the date on which World War II began or ended, this is the period most frequently cited.
2.  **[^](#cite_ref-2)** Often abbreviated as **WWII** or **WW2**
3.  **[^](#cite_ref-73)** [The UK declared war on Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom_declaration_of_war_on_Germany_\(1939\) "United Kingdom declaration of war on Germany (1939)") at 11 am. [France followed 6 hours later](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_declaration_of_war_on_Germany_\(1939\) "French declaration of war on Germany (1939)") at 5 pm.
4.  **[^](#cite_ref-373)** Reparations were exacted from [East Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Germany "East Germany"), [Hungary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungarian_People%27s_Republic "Hungarian People's Republic"), [Romania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romanian_People%27s_Republic "Romanian People's Republic"), and [Bulgaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Bulgaria "People's Republic of Bulgaria") using Soviet-dominated joint enterprises. The Soviet Union also instituted trading arrangements deliberately designed to favour the country. Moscow controlled the Communist parties that ruled the satellite states, and they followed orders from the Kremlin. Historian Mark Kramer concludes: "The net outflow of resources from eastern Europe to the Soviet Union was approximately $15 billion to $20 billion in the first decade after World War II, an amount roughly equal to the total aid provided by the United States to western Europe under the [Marshall Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marshall_Plan "Marshall Plan")."

71.  **[^](#cite_ref-Keegan_1997_35_74-0)** [Keegan 1997](#CITEREFKeegan1997), p. 35.  
     [Cienciala 2010](#CITEREFCienciala2010), p. 128, observes that, while it is true that Poland was far away, making it difficult for the French and British to provide support, "\[f\]ew Western historians of World War II ... know that the British had committed to bomb Germany if it attacked Poland, but did not do so except for one raid on the base of Wilhelmshaven. The French, who committed to attacking Germany in the west, had no intention of doing so."

272.  **[^](#cite_ref-275)** [Holland 2008](#CITEREFHolland2008), pp. 169–184; [Beevor 2012](#CITEREFBeevor2012), pp. 568–573.  
      The weeks after the fall of Rome saw a dramatic upswing in German atrocities in Italy ([Mazower 2008](#CITEREFMazower2008), pp. 500–502). The period featured massacres with victims in the hundreds at [Civitella](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civitella_in_Val_di_Chiana "Civitella in Val di Chiana") ([de Grazia & Paggi 1991](#CITEREFde_GraziaPaggi1991); [Belco 2010](#CITEREFBelco2010)), [Fosse Ardeatine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ardeatine_massacre "Ardeatine massacre") ([Portelli 2003](#CITEREFPortelli2003)), and [Sant'Anna di Stazzema](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sant%27Anna_di_Stazzema_massacre "Sant'Anna di Stazzema massacre") ([Gordon 2012](#CITEREFGordon2012), pp. 10–11), and is capped with the [Marzabotto massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marzabotto_massacre "Marzabotto massacre").

320.  **[^](#cite_ref-Pape_1993_323-0)** [Pape 1993](#CITEREFPape1993) "The principal cause of Japan's surrender was the ability of the United States to increase the military vulnerability of Japan's home islands, persuading Japanese leaders that defence of the homeland was highly unlikely to succeed. The key military factor causing this effect was the sea blockade, which crippled Japan's ability to produce and equip the forces necessary to execute its strategy. The most important factor accounting for the timing of surrender was the Soviet attack against Manchuria, largely because it persuaded previously adamant Army leaders that the homeland could not be defended".

Nearly 100,000 additional murders of psychiatric patients occurred in occupied or annexed territories. Around one-third of the patient murders in the Reich took place during the so-called T4 program in its first, centrally directed phase.\]
